Important News

Shanghai Scout Inspection and Camp 36

More than 2,000 Scouts Participated... Excellent Form and Spirit

The third Shanghai Scout inspection and camp of the Chinese Boy Scouts was held yesterday at the Longhua training ground. Scouts from 29 schools, including Patriotic Girls' School, Guangzhao Public School, and China Women's Physical Education School, participated, totaling more than 2,000 people. The weather was clear and the breeze was gentle. The Scouts were full of spirit and neatly dressed. The form and substance were excellent, fully demonstrating the spirit of Shanghai education. The details of the inspection are recorded as follows:

Participating Schools

The names and troop numbers of the Scout schools participating in the inspection and camp are as follows: 7th Troop: Patriotic Girls' School, 15th Troop: Guangzhao Public School, 20th Troop: China Women's Physical Education School, 64th Troop: Jinan University, 65th Troop: Commercial Press, 113th Troop: Xiang Sheng Iron Factory Workers' Children's School, 121st Troop: Southeast Women's Physical Education School, 129th Troop: British American Tobacco Factory Workers' Children's School, 176th Troop: Youth Moral Education Association, 177th Troop: Guangzhao Free School, 178th Troop: Ningbo Shanghai First Primary School, 179th Troop: Ningbo Shanghai Second Primary School, 196th Troop: Liangjiang Women's Physical Education School, 213th Troop: Yucai Middle School, 214th Troop: Guangdong Primary and Secondary School, 221st Troop: Fudan University High School Affiliated, 230th Troop: Shanghai Middle School Experimental Primary School, 247th Troop: Xinlonghua Art School, 250th Troop: East Asia Physical Education School, 251st Troop: Middle School Physical Education School, 254th Troop: Chengzhong Middle School, 268th Troop: Fudan Middle School, 270th Troop: Moore Memorial Church, 299th Troop: Lizhi Primary School, 308th Troop: Pudong Middle School, 349th Troop: Shanghai Middle School, 352nd Troop: Meixi Primary School, 383rd Troop: Guanghua University High School Affiliated, 50th Troop: Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

Inspection Staff

The list of staff members for the grand inspection is as follows: Presidium: Zhang Qun, Tong Xingbai, Xu Peihuang; General Commander: Shen Yu; Deputy General Commanders: Wang Gang, Leng Xueqiao; Sub-Commanders: Yu Kuiming, Sun Yixin, Qu Yue; Chairman: Zhang Qun; Deputy Director: Tong Xingbai, Shen Yu; General Affairs Section: Wang Gang, Yu Kuiming; Inspection Section: Gu Zhengcai, Leng Xueqiao; Camping Section: Zhang Xunfang, Sun Yixin; Assessment Section: Xu Peihuang, Xu Zicheng.

Venue Setup

The inspection venue was located at the Longhua training ground. At the entrance, there was a memorial archway made of sorghum and cypress trees with the inscription "Third Grand Inspection and Camp of the Chinese Boy Scouts." The entire venue was surrounded by rope walls with Scouts on sentry duty, maintaining strict security. A review stand was set up on the north side of the venue, with prizes displayed on the table. The offices of the various sections were on the left side of the stand. The Scout camps of each school were arranged around the perimeter of the venue. Each school's camp gate was decorated with fresh flowers and cypress trees, or with artistic designs, creating a solemn atmosphere.

Yesterday's Order

(1) Entry (music played), (2) Flag raising, (3) Singing the party song, (4) Paying the highest respect to the national flag and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen in the auditorium, (5) Reading Sun Yat-sen's last will and testament, (6) Paying the highest respect to the martyrs of the May 3rd Incident, (7) Three minutes of silence, (8) Offering flowers to the martyrs of the May 3rd Massacre, (9) Grand inspection (music played): A. Parade: (1) Reporting the number of people, (2) Inspection, (3) Basic movements, (4) Simulated attack; B. Marching: (1) Command to start, (2) The entire group marches around the venue in front of the inspection stand, (10) Report, (11) Address, (12) Singing the Scout song, (13) Ceremony concludes.

Attending Guests

More than 100 guests attended, including Lai Weiying, Chief of Staff of the Songhu Garrison Command; Jiang Yi, Adjutant; Zhou Jisheng, representative of the municipal government; Tong Xingbai, representative of the municipal party headquarters; Xu Peihuang, Director of the Education Bureau; Mo Weiqiang, representative of the Social Affairs Bureau; Shi Youcai, representative of the China National Aviation Corporation; Wang Jingseng of the Shanghai South District Security Corps, and representatives from various schools.

Inspection Details

At 10:00 AM, all the inspection troops had already formed up. Wearing military uniforms and carrying sticks, they marched in formation. The sound of trumpets and the sight of flags shook the mountains. After the formation was completed, the General Commander ordered the flag to be raised. The national flag rose in the center of the venue, and the military music competed. The entire venue stood solemnly and stared, showing the utmost respect. After the ceremony, the grand inspection began. The troops marched around the venue in single file, paying attention to the inspection stand. After each troop finished performing, they lined up under the stand and received an address.

Chairman's Report

Tong Xingbai of the Presidium reported that the Scouts in the city are usually located in various schools or organizations and have few opportunities to learn from each other. Therefore, the purpose of holding the grand inspection is to allow each other to learn from each other and to demonstrate the skills and techniques learned in peacetime. Although the city has held two inspections, they have all relied on the leadership of the party and government organs. This is the first time that the Scouts have taken action on their own. The achievements of the Shanghai Scouts today are all due to the support of the party and government organs. Therefore, the Scouts should continue to work hard and not disappoint the expectations of all parties.

Mayor's Speech

Mayor Zhang was in Beijing today and was represented by Luo Jingyou, Chief of the Second Section, who delivered a speech stating that in addition to the general significance, this grand inspection of the Scouts also has a significant meaning, which is that it coincides with the May 3rd Memorial and the upcoming opening of the National Assembly. The former is due to weakness and humiliation, while the latter is the future vitality of China. Both revenge and construction depend on organized and heroic Scouts.

Address from the Party Headquarters

Tong Xingbai, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, delivered an address stating that during the International Scout Competition held in the past two months, the performances fully exposed the brutality of imperialism in humiliating weak nations. The true meaning of Scouting is selflessness, not oppression by the powerful. From a negative perspective, one should not have a desire for revenge. From a positive perspective, one should deeply remember to work hard and strive forward.

Guest Speeches

Lai Weiying, Chief of Staff of the Songhu Garrison Command, gave a speech stating that although countries around the world are talking about peace, they are expanding their military preparations. The world is not truly peaceful. One must have considerable military strength to survive. The essence of the army is the people. If the people are good, then the army is good. This responsibility rests on today's Scouts.

Education Director's Speech

Xu Peihuang, Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, gave a speech stating that the elements of Scouting are discipline, courtesy, martial spirit, and adherence to discipline. If one adheres to discipline, then the law will not be chaotic. If one values courtesy, then people will do their jobs well. If one values martial spirit, then one will not be humiliated. The responsibility of the Scouts is to change customs and habits. After the speech, it was 12:00 noon, and photos were taken and everyone rested. At 2:00 PM, various skills were demonstrated again, and it ended at 5:00 PM. The campfire was originally scheduled for last night, but due to the May 3rd Memorial, it was not appropriate to show mourning, so it was changed to tonight.

Commercial News

Last Week's Call Money Was Slightly Better 40

Market Sentiment Remains Hesitant and Anxious. Last week's call money showed a slight upward trend. Although the state of affairs was hesitant and there were no special changes, the price of silver still lingered around 740 taels outside of 10 taels. Large clients were seeking supply from various sources. The lowest price on Tuesday was 728.9 taels, which was likely due to the ease in the exchange rate. By Friday, Guangbang Hengxingsheng made a large purchase to offset its short position, suddenly breaking through the 50-tael mark, reaching 53.5 taels. There was also a difference of 24.6 taels. As a result, the market weakened again, settling at 44.7 taels, with a total increase of only 3.9 taels. In short, market sentiment was hesitant and uncertain. As for the overseas silver market, it fell slightly, with the price of large bars decreasing by 0.25 and the price of silver decreasing by 0.25. However, the exchange rate of Shanghai's British silver decreased by only half a notch (0.125). The exchange rate of Japanese gold increased by 0.0125. The stagnation of bank transactions was also evident. Chinese gold businesses were scrambling to settle their accounts to offset their previous short positions, and they were using receipts to cover their positions. It is estimated that more than ten taels of profit could be made. According to various firms, they are gradually settling their positions, and they are now almost breaking even. The total amount of receipts in the exchange recently is estimated to be around 46,000 to 47,000. Guangbang, such as Hengxingsheng, Dafeng, Yongda, Xingyong, Tianyu, Yongbingxing, Qianchangxiang, Cuichangyong, and Fuchang, are all long. The Central Bank also seems to be long. Wu has been gradually releasing a lot of gold, but he does not have many assets in hand. Xinxingyuansheng has few long positions, and they are mostly short. The goods are being used for hedging, and the spot houses such as Yingfeng, Hengdafeng, and Heng are also short. However, the price of spot silver has increased by more than 7 taels compared to the call money. Observing the situation, the future price of gold is likely to increase. The general situation of the week is recorded below:

Fluctuating Supply and Demand, Relatively Stable. On Monday (April 27), there was no change in the price of large bars and exchange rates. However, the domestic market showed signs of easing, so gold prices fell. Firms sold their positions. The initial price was 740.05 taels, a decrease of 0.03 taels. The price then increased from 38.5 taels to 41.7 taels. Later, the supply of large clients exceeded the demand, and Jinan's agent, He, sold off his positions, causing the price to drop by more than 8 taels. The market closed at 31.8 taels, a decrease of 9 taels compared to Saturday. The price difference in the city was 10.07 taels. The next day, the price of large bars increased by 0.125, and the price of silver increased by 0.25. As a result, the exchange rate increased by one notch. The internal market was tight, so firms first sold and then bought. The opening price of call money was flat at 32 taels. Although the price of large bars increased, it was not enough. The price was 34 taels. Later, large clients sold off their positions, and the exchange rate suddenly broke through the 30-tael mark, reaching 28.9 taels. Suddenly, the Central Bank came in to buy, and Dayu, Yong and other firms kept buying, causing the price to increase by more than 8 taels. Wu also chased the price upwards. The price reached 40.05 taels in the afternoon. The market closed at 37.8 taels, an increase of 6 taels compared to the previous day. The total increase was 11.6 taels. Looking back on Wednesday, the price of large bars decreased by 0.125, and the price of American silver decreased by 0.25. Therefore, the exchange rate decreased by half a notch. Hedging firms bought positions. The price of gold was 38 taels, then 33 taels, because Wu released his positions. It was rumored that the Central Bank planned to buy cash for the preparation of customs gold coins, so market sentiment was boosted, and the price broke through the 40-tael mark, reaching 44 taels. In the afternoon, sellers were abundant, and the exchange rate turned flat. The market closed at 38 taels, a slight increase of 0.02 taels compared to the previous day. The price fluctuated by 11 taels. The next day, the price of large bars was stable. The initial exchange rate did not change. In the afternoon, the exchange rate suddenly decreased by half a notch. The domestic market strengthened again, and firms rushed to buy. The opening price of call money was 38.3 taels, then 36 taels, because the private telegram silver price increased by 0.125. Buyers entered the market, and the price escaped the 40-tael mark. In the afternoon, Daxingyong offset Hengxingsheng's short positions, reaching 48.5 taels. The price then decreased to 43.5 taels due to the impact of the decline in public bonds. The market closed at 47.2 taels, a further increase of 9.2 taels compared to the previous day. The total difference for the day was 12.5 taels, and Hengxingsheng bought 4,000 to 5,000 receipts. On Friday, the price of large bars decreased by 0.0625, the price of silver decreased by half a cent, and the exchange rate decreased by half a notch. The domestic market was tighter than before, and firms settled their accounts. The opening price of call money was 49.5 taels, an increase of 2.3 taels. The price then decreased to 47.1 taels. Later, Hengxingsheng bought many positions, reaching 52 taels. Wu and other large clients sold off their positions, and the air was bad. The wind turned sharply downwards. In the afternoon, the price was 42 taels. Hengxingsheng and Wu bought again, and the price rose to 52.3 taels. The market closed at 52.3 taels, an increase of 5.1 taels for four consecutive days (a total of 20.05 taels). The total price difference for the market was 11.5 taels. On Saturday, the price of large bars decreased by 0.1875, the price of American silver increased by 0.25, and the exchange rate did not change. The domestic market seemed to be increasing. The opening price of call money was 48.5 taels, a decrease of 3.8 taels. The price then decreased to 40 taels. Later, the price rose and fell by 2 to 3 taels. Yesterday was Sunday, and all Chinese and foreign banks were closed as usual. There were no reports on the financial and foreign exchange markets. Another Penny Plus on Foreign Exchange 42

Foreign Exchange Rates Have Been Rising Continuously. The Market Is Quite Good Because of Good Sales. Wuyuan North Road Head Tea Is Being Picked 50

The Tea Farmers in Wuyi County Pre-Picked and Made the Early Tea Dew Buds, Which Were Slightly Longer, Because the Old Grass Was Exempted From Price Reduction and the Stagnant Sales. Except for Chizhanjian Yanchuan East Road and Other Places That Were Opened for Mining Some Time Ago, Yesterday, North Road Sikou, Sixi, Jinzhu, Longla, Zhangcun, and Other Places Also Hired Workers to Start Enclosing. The Thin and Tender Head of the Tea Body After Production Has Not Been Seen in Decades. If Early and Late Tea Leaves Are Picked Early According to This, the Output Will Inevitably Be A Big Loss. According to the Tea Made Recently, It Is Picked 10 Days Earlier Than in Previous Years. Each Tea Tree Clump Needs to Be Lost by 40%. However, the Tea Number Is Very Happy to See This Improvement Method. It Is Expected That the Finished Boxes Will Be Shipped to Shanghai in the Future, Which Can Invite Foreign Gao Le to Purchase.

67 Tea Numbers Have Been Reduced in Tunxi 51

Recently, the New Tea From Various Tea Numbers in Tunbu Has Been Picked and Will Be on the Market Soon. Moreover, Various Tea Numbers Believe That the Mountain Price This Year Will Be Reduced, and the Tea Body Will Be Shipped With Tender Heads, Manual Labor and Sundries Are All Slightly Cheaper Than Before. They Believe That It Is A Great Opportunity. The Original Tea Numbers That Planned Not to Open the Scale and Suspend Operations Are Now Moving Their Index Fingers. It Seems That They Are Eager to Try. Because the Tea Market Needs Money, Qian Zhuang Has Been Transporting Two Batches From Shanghai and Hangzhou for Several Days. The Current Ocean Has More Than 100,000 Silver Roots, Which Is More Smooth Than Before. The Total Number of New and Old Tea Numbers in Tunbu, Shuikou, and Yanghu That Have Decided to Suspend Operations Is Only 67. The Rest Have Already Opened the Scale Early and Are Trying to Open the Scale. There Is Still Some Optimism About the Future of the Tea Market.

Tea Numbers Also Have No Desire to Increase the Burden Because They Have Not Sold the Old Tea Left in Shanghai. Page 13

Local News

Abolish the Right of Consular Jurisdiction 54

The Sino-British Negotiations Broke Down

Disagreement on the Fourth Point

It Seems Unlikely That It Will Reopen for A While.

Reuters, Shanghai, 3rd Reuters has learned that the UK and other relevant countries have put forward the following four points in the negotiations with China on the issue of consular jurisdiction: (1) Cases involving the people of relevant countries that are adjudicated by Chinese courts may be referred to foreign courts of relevant countries; (2) Relevant countries will give up their right of consular jurisdiction, starting with civil cases and slowing down with criminal cases; (3) Chinese special courts will hire foreign consultants to hear foreign cases; (4) The region within fifty miles of Shanghai, Guangzhou, Tianjin and Hankou will still maintain consular jurisdiction for several years. After long-term negotiations, the UK has cancelled the first three points, but insisted on the fourth point. The Chinese government has never agreed to it, so Foreign Minister Wang's negotiations with British Minister Lan broke down, and it seems unlikely that negotiations will reopen for a while.

All Sectors of This City Tomorrow 55

Celebrate the Opening of the National Congress

Location: Shanghai Chamber of Commerce

Time is Set for 9:00 AM

And Stipulated Nine Game Venues

Tomorrow, the 5th, is the first day of the opening of the National Congress. All sectors of the city have been actively preparing for the celebration beforehand, and it has been published in various newspapers. However, that day happens to be the tenth anniversary of the establishment of the National Government, so representatives from all sectors who attend the event are bound to participate enthusiastically. The Heavenly Queen Palace Shanghai Chamber of Commerce has been selected to hold the Shanghai All Sectors Celebration of the National Congress Opening Ceremony and the National Government's Tenth Anniversary Commemoration Meeting, and nine recreational venues have been stipulated. The details are as follows:

The Presidium of the Congress The Presidium of the Congress consists of Yu Hongjun, Xiong Shihui, Yang Qingyuan, Zhu Yingpeng, Lu Jingshi, Ye Huijun, Lin Kecong, and other seven people.

Order of the Congress (1) All stand at attention (2) Play music (3) Sing the Party Song (4) Pay the highest respect to the Party, the national flag, and the portrait of the Premier (5) Read the Premier's will respectfully (6) Remain silent (7) The Chairman reports (8) Speech (9) Shout slogans (10) Play music (11) Dismiss the meeting

Slogans of the Congress (1) Convening the National Congress is to carry out the teachings of the Premier (2) Convening the National Congress is to consolidate national unity (3) Convening the National Congress is to seek national construction (4) Unify the national democracy (5) Consolidate the revolutionary foundation (6) Formulate a covenant that the people of the country believe in and abide by together (7) Abolish consular jurisdiction (8) Recover all concessions in the country (9) Abolish all unequal treaties (10) Eradicate all reactionaries (11) Support the National Congress (12) Long live the Chinese Kuomintang (13) Long live the Republic of China (14) Long live the National Congress

Recreational Venues There are nine major recreational venues in this city to celebrate the National Congress. The first recreational venue is the recreational congress of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. The second recreational venue is the Da Guangming Grand Theater. The third recreational venue is the Xin Guang Grand Theater. The fourth recreational venue is the Penglai Grand Theater. The fifth recreational venue is the World Grand Theater. The sixth recreational venue is the Southeast Grand Theater. The seventh recreational venue is the Small World. The eighth recreational venue is the Immortal World. The ninth recreational venue is the Bansong Garden. There are performances by various famous recreational groups and song and dance groups. Each theater will screen blockbusters to celebrate.

Promotional Publications There are more than a dozen types of promotional items, including commemorative special publications for the celebration of the National Congress and leaflets and slogans, with rich content and beautiful forms. All those who participate in the commemoration meeting will receive a copy per person.

Various Places 56

National Congress Representatives Arrive in Beijing

The Grand Occasion of Reception and Farewell

In recent days, many representatives of the National Congress elected by various provinces have arrived in Shanghai. It is learned that the representatives took the Shanghai Express attached to the special train for representatives of the National Congress to Beijing yesterday, one after another, because the conference is about to officially open tomorrow. The details are as follows:

Colorful Arches Built at the North Station The Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Administration built a colorful arch at the open space outside the gate of the station in order to accommodate the large number of representatives from various provinces to Beijing for this National Congress. The words "Celebrating the National Congress" were written on white cloth and decorated with paper flowers and lit with electric torches. In addition, the Railway Administration also hung flags and lanterns at the entrance, and pasted strips of paper with the words "Welcome National Congress Representatives" and "Welcome Farewell" on white bamboo cloth in various places. A reception office named "National Congress Reception Office of the Two Railways" was also set up in the first and second class passenger waiting rooms, and various groups of staff were assigned to show seriousness.

Representatives Arrive in Beijing One After Another Yesterday and the day before yesterday, Wu Kaixian, Hu Shuhua, Hou Dachun, Chen Guansheng, Wang Yansong, and others from this city went to Beijing one after another. Others include Sun Xintian (representative of Weihaiwei), Pan Qijun (representative of the Gansu Provincial Chamber of Commerce), Zhang Naiyan (representative of Zhejiang Province), Qin Liankui (representative of the Jiangsu Provincial Farmers Association), 23 representatives from Guangdong, eight representatives from Guangxi, nine representatives from Yunnan, and one representative each from Sichuan and overseas Chinese in Chile. Many people went to the station to see them off. The representatives bid farewell with precious handshakes amidst the fluttering flags and the melodious military music.

The Beijing Reception Office is Established The National Congress Representative Reception Office issued a notice yesterday stating that the office has been organized and established in the Biology Museum of Chengxian Street Central University, and reception offices have been set up in the Grand Hotel of the Xiaguan Station and the Daxin Hotel in Jiangkou. All representatives who come to Beijing are requested to contact the reception office first so that staff can be assigned to take care of them. If they enter the city directly without contacting the office, please notify the office directly, for fear of not being aware of it. This is hereby notified.

Cars are Transported to Beijing for Application The central government, fearing that the vehicles in the capital would be insufficient due to the arrival of representatives from various provinces, ordered a special commissioner to come to Shanghai to contact the Shanghai Automobile Association to draw 100 cars from various car companies for application. At 1:00 am yesterday, 50 cars were transported by the Shanghai-Ning Special Train first, and 50 more cars were transported later.

Public Times Middle School 57

Commemorating the May 3rd Massacre

Chairman Wang Jingqi Reports

Mrs. Cai's Voice Filled with Tears

Yesterday was the third anniversary of the Jinan Massacre. Public Times Middle School in the Japanese Concession held a memorial meeting at the school playground in the morning. Guests included representatives from the Municipal Party Committee, Zhou Hanmei; representatives from the Municipal Education Bureau, Cen Dezhang; school board members such as Wang Jingqi; and all faculty and students of the school. The meeting began at 10:00 AM, presided over by Chairman Wang Jingqi, with Qin Hegao as the master of ceremonies and Zeng Yaozhang as the recorder. The ceremony was conducted solemnly. First, the chairman reported on the significance of commemorating May 3rd, stating briefly, "When the Jinan Incident occurred three years ago, I was attending a League of Nations meeting in Switzerland. Although there were foreign reports about the case, I was still very doubtful. Only when I received domestic telegrams did I learn the truth of the case, and I was extremely indignant. I originally planned to submit this case to the League of Nations for a fair judgment, but due to other diplomatic issues, I was unable to fulfill my wish, which I deeply regret. I deeply feel that there are three periods in life: past, present, and future. Mr. Gongshi is worthy of our commemoration today because of his great integrity and ability to uphold justice. Our school was founded to commemorate Mr. Gongshi. I hope that students will have good morals and profound knowledge, and serve the country and society in the future to achieve the goal of avenging our humiliation, and not disappoint Mrs. Cai's aspiration to establish schools." Next, Zhou Hanmei, representative of the Municipal Party Committee, gave a speech, stating briefly, "We really did not expect that the Japanese would dare to be so bold as to kill our compatriots in Jinan, massacre our diplomats, and murder martyrs like Cai Gongshi. Even more unexpectedly, the League of Nations showed no reaction to this tragedy. Therefore, we can think of the pity of 'weak countries having no diplomacy' and should determine our future direction of effort. First, we hope to have a unified and strong government to resist the aggression of imperialism and to handle the general construction of China. Second, we hope that the students of Public Times Middle School will take advantage of this promising period of youth to study hard and cultivate themselves quietly in preparation for avenging our humiliation in the future." Then, Cen Dezhang, representative of the Education Bureau, gave a speech, stating briefly, "Today, the whole country commemorates May 3rd, but the most grievous commemoration is here. However, the best way to commemorate Mr. Gongshi is to establish a middle school, because middle school is the foundation of university. If we want to avenge our humiliation, we must first have profound knowledge. Mrs. Cai's founding of Gongshi School, starting with education to achieve the purpose of avenging humiliation, is extremely correct. I hope that all students and faculty will work together to live up to Mrs. Cai's aspirations." Then, guest Xing Yichun and student representatives gave speeches successively. Finally, Mrs. Cai thanked the guests for their guidance and reported on the tragic experience of the Jinan Massacre at that time. Her voice was filled with tears, and the whole audience was extremely sad and indignant, especially many students were in tears. Afterwards, she reported on the process of going to Jinan to investigate the remains of martyr Cai and others, and said that she would still have to go to Jinan after this painful memorial day. It was already after 1:00 PM, so a photo was taken and the meeting adjourned.

Promotion in This City 58

New Weights and Measures System

The Public Security and Social Affairs Bureaus Jointly Issue a Proclamation Yesterday

The promotion of the new weights and measures system in this city has been set for completion by July 1 of this year. The Social Affairs Bureau has already submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for approval. As the deadline is very near, it should be actively promoted. Yesterday, the Social Affairs and Public Security Bureaus jointly issued a proclamation and attached six articles of Chapter 13 of the Criminal Law on the crime of counterfeiting weights and measures to serve as a warning. The original text is as follows: "For the matter of jointly issuing a proclamation, the promotion of the new weights and measures system in this city is scheduled to be completed by July 1 of this year. The Social Affairs Bureau has submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for approval. As the deadline for unification is very short, the weights and measures used in various industries in this city should be actively promoted in accordance with the new system so that they can be unified on schedule. The weighing instruments used in various markets are uneven. Now that the new system is being promoted, it is appropriate to reform them first to benefit the people's livelihood and demonstrate fairness. In addition to ordering all manufacturers and shops in the city to prohibit the manufacture of old instruments and reformulate new instruments, those who violate it will be severely punished. The joint proclamation is issued to all markets for their knowledge, and they should abolish all old instruments and implement the new system uniformly from June 1 of this year. Those who dare to violate it will be dealt with in accordance with Chapter 13 of the Criminal Law on the crime of counterfeiting weights and measures. Do not violate this. In addition, if the markets need the aforementioned new instruments, they can directly inquire at the Shanghai Weights and Measures Verification Institute on Xieqiao Manufacturing Bureau Road. This announcement is attached with Chapter 13 of the Criminal Law on the crime of counterfeiting weights and measures. Article 218: Those who intend to manufacture weights and measures that violate the prescribed procedures or change the prescribed procedures of weights and measures for the purpose of exercising them shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not more than one year or detention, and may also be fined or converted into a fine of not more than 300 yuan. The attempted crime of this article shall be punished. Article 219: Those who intend to sell weights and measures that violate the prescribed procedures for the purpose of exercising them shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not more than one year or detention, and may also be fined or converted into a fine of not more than 300 yuan. The attempted crime of this article shall be punished. Article 220: Those who exercise weights and measures that violate the prescribed procedures shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not more than two years or detention, and may also be fined or converted into a fine of not more than 1,000 yuan. The attempted crime of this article shall be punished. Article 221: Those who intend to hold weights and measures that violate the prescribed procedures for the purpose of exercising them shall be fined not more than 100 yuan. Article 222: The weights and measures that violate the prescribed procedures in the preceding article shall be confiscated regardless of whether they belong to the offender. Article 223: Those who commit the crimes in this chapter may be deprived of their civil rights in accordance with the provisions of Articles 57 and 58. April, 20th year of the Republic of China. Director of the Public Security Bureau, Chen Xizeng. Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, Pan Gongzhan."

As for the security problem in the province, I am entrusted by the elders. Once I arrive in Beijing, no matter how difficult it is, I will try to submit it to the authorities for relief so that I will not fail the elders' expectations." At that time, the glasses clinked and the toasts were exchanged until 9:15 PM, and everyone dispersed happily.

Inspection of Foreigners' Entry 63

Six Ships Arrived in the Past Two Days

All Were Found to Have Passports

The Municipal Public Security Bureau was ordered to implement the inspection of foreigners' entry passports from May 1st. The inspection has been quite busy these days. The various situations are recorded as follows:

Inspection Procedures: For ships carrying passengers arriving at the first port of Shanghai from overseas (including Hong Kong and Dalian), except for Japanese people who are exempt from inspection due to the Sino-Japanese mutual agreement, the medical officers of the National Quarantine Office first board the ship for inspection, followed by the inspectors of the Passport Inspection Office of the Public Security Bureau, and then the Jianghai Customs inspects prohibited items. No one is allowed to disembark during the inspection, which is very strict. Those who are found to have no passports will be prohibited from landing. If the passport lacks the signature of the Chinese envoy, they must go to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to complete the signature.

Internal Organization: The Passport Inspection Office of the Municipal Public Security Bureau is headed by Hong Qi, with Chen Timing as the deputy director. The inspectors are Zhang Feifan, Zheng Zhong, Zhang Xiuhuai, Zhou Yizu, Shao Renlun, Hong Sen, Yao Changzhen, Ou Qiliang, Zhang Desheng, Du Mao, Zhou Chunyu, Li Guangshun, Yuan Ji, Ding He, Zhou Xinyuan, and others, totaling 15 people. All of them are section members of the Public Security Bureau who have been selected by the director for their high academic achievements and graduation from universities or specialized schools, and who are proficient in several languages. They are divided into groups of five and go to inspect the ships as soon as they arrive, regardless of the night. For the convenience of inspection, a temporary office is set up at No. 9 Hankou Road and in the Wusong Ning Shang Fire Brigade. Office hours are from 6:00 AM to 10:00 PM.

Situation in the Past Two Days: On the previous day (2nd), the foreign merchant ships that arrived in Shanghai were (1) the Beide Company's Diweisi Fort, which arrived at 11:00 AM and berthed at the Gonghexiang Wharf, (2) the Gleniffer, which sailed from London, England, and arrived at 10:00 AM and berthed at the Zhaoshang North Bund, and (3) the Osaka Company's Nagasaki Maru, which arrived at 3:00 PM and berthed at the Huishan Wharf. Yesterday (3rd), the ships that arrived in Shanghai were (1) the British Company's Cleanthe, which arrived at 10:00 AM and berthed at buoys No. 4 and 5, (2) the Osaka Company's Shengjing Maru, which arrived at 10:00 AM and berthed at the Yangshupu Wharf, and (3) the Java Company's Java, which arrived at 3:00 PM and berthed at the Zhaoshang Middle Bund. After sending personnel to inspect them separately, it was found that none of them had passports. Although a few people lacked the signature of the Chinese envoy due to the tight schedule, the inspectors immediately led them to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to complete the signature.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce 65

Requests Strict Prohibition of Japanese Fish Sales

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday requested the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to thoroughly investigate and strictly prohibit Japanese ships from fishing beyond the border and encroaching on our country's territorial waters. The original report stated that Member Jin Chuxiang requested that the import of fish by Japanese ships be stopped and that our country's fishing industry be protected. The Ministry telegraphed an order on February 13 of this year, which was approved by the Ministry of Finance. According to the report from the Zhejiang Customs, Japanese fishing boats do not declare the import of fish. The original report and order were forwarded for your information. Later, on March 3, Jin Chuxiang continued to state that Japanese ships fishing beyond the sea have been reported in newspapers more than once. Chuxiang was born in a fishing village and is familiar with the fishing industry. Because he recognized the failure of the fishing industry in recent years and the encroachment on maritime rights by imperialists, he shouted loudly and requested the Chamber of Commerce to forward the report to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for verification and handling in order to save the fishing industry and fight for national rights. Unexpectedly, the authorities only relied on the Zhejiang Customs to recognize that Japanese fishing boats do not declare the import of fish, and dismissed the report as not matching the facts reported by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and did not thoroughly investigate whether there were any Japanese fishing boats entering other ports. Chuxiang believed that it was a perfunctory matter, because the Japanese are cunning and often collude with Chinese traitors to deceive and conceal the import of fish. Therefore, tax declarations are often concealed. Recently, the Daiseimaru, Takakumo Maru, and Hakuyo Maru, three fishing boats managed by the Japanese merchant Rin-yu Company, were transported to Xiaodongmen in Shanghai to sell Chinese fish in large quantities. The facts are all there. Please send personnel to thoroughly investigate and clarify to dispel doubts and save fish merchants. It was immediately ordered that personnel be dispatched to investigate and found that the import of fish by the Japanese has been going on for a long time. However, the products imported have always been Qingchuan salmon and other products, as well as yellow croaker, shark, and beltfish. According to the report, these types of fish are produced in the seas of Jiangzhe under the jurisdiction of Sheshan Langgang Reef. Foreigners are now importing this type of fish, which is abnormal. However, there is no basis to know whether the Japanese are fishing within our country's maritime rights or outside the border. It is only known that they are packed and transported to China and docked in the Yangshupu area, where they evade taxes and sell them to vendors. Merchants profit from their low prices and compete to purchase them. Half of them are sold to small vegetable market stalls and half are sold to fresh fish shops. Later, this case was reported in the newspapers, and all sectors opposed it strongly. Therefore, the Japanese ships slightly reduced their activities, and imports have gradually decreased recently. It was also stated that there are companies such as the Da Zhonghua Company that organize their own rounds for procurement, and there are also companies with complete Chinese capital that hire Japanese people to rent Japanese ships. However, the Japanese collude with traitors to seek profits, and it is difficult to distinguish the truth in this. Recently, the fishery improvement association's publicity has called for fishery administration agencies to actively prevent or possibly save the situation. Based on this, the damage caused by Japanese ships fishing beyond the border and encroaching on our country's territorial waters and the methods of prevention have been detailed in the telegram of the Association last November, and we have been granted an investigation. According to the investigation, Japanese fish are sold in this city, and there are Japanese colluding with traitors. Although all sectors and fishery groups oppose it, it is not effective unless the competent authorities strictly prohibit it. It is reasonable to telegraph the Ministry for inspection and approval to thoroughly investigate and strictly prohibit it without any leniency to maintain the fishery for public convenience.

Jiangsu and Zhejiang Fishery Association, Wu Zhenpan; Jiangsu and Zhejiang Fishing Vessel Association, Xu Yifei; Fishery Merchants Ge Liqing, Lin Meiqing, Zhou Meiting, etc.

Various Industries Tax Rules Association 67

Continues to Submit Opinions on Business Tax

The tax rules research committee of the various industries' trade associations in Shanghai previously forwarded the opinions of the dried longan industry and the native cloth industry on the business tax rate in Shanghai to the Municipal Government for adoption. Recently, the association has received opinions from various industries' trade associations.

Page 14

May 4th, 20th year of the Republic of China (Fourth Sheet of the Shen Bao) Monday (40)

After further research, the association believes that they should be revised. Yesterday, it submitted the revised text to the Municipal Government for further action. The opinions submitted by the association are recorded as follows: 1. The purpose of the taxi industry is to serve the society and facilitate transportation, and foreign merchants and colleagues are mixed in it. The rate of taxation should be specially reduced and calculated at one-thousandth of the capital to facilitate promotion. 2. The Chinese and Western furniture industry's business is all furniture supplies, and raw materials such as ziji, mahogany, teak, liuan, and masuli, and accessories such as paoli paint, glass, hinges, and hardware, etc., are directly and indirectly subject to business tax. The burden is already excessive and should be reviewed and reduced to two-thousandths of the business tax of the industry. 3. The restaurant industry and the teahouse industry's business is all to supply food, which is the same nature as the cake industry and the noodle industry. The business tax rate in this city is two-thousandths for the cake industry and the qushi industry, while it is five-thousandths for the restaurant industry and the teahouse industry. The difference in weight is obvious and should be reduced to two-thousandths to show equality. 4. The silver cabinet industry's business contains manufacturing properties. Zhejiang Province's business tax has been taxed according to the capital. This city cannot be unique and should be taxed according to the capital as in Zhejiang Province. 5. The department store industry's best-selling items are socks, followed by cotton textiles, etc. Cosmetics and miscellaneous goods account for only one-tenth or two-tenths of the total amount. Although the store names are named after the company sock factory, the actual business is the sales agency of various woven products. The recent draft of the business tax rate table in this city taxes five-thousandths, while the revised business tax collection regulations of the Ministry of Finance for Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces stipulate that if a store has several businesses with different tax rates, the tax amount should be calculated based on the main part of its business. Then, the business tax of the industry should not exceed two-thousandths to avoid inequality and comply with the provisions of the regulations. 6. The blasting industry's business tax is proposed to be ten-thousandths in the draft business tax in this city, while the tax rates set by Hunan and Anhui provinces are both two-thousandths. It should be reduced in accordance with the precedent to show support for manual labor. 7. The business tax rate for the flower and tree industry and the watch industry in this city's draft business tax is ten-thousandths. In terms of their nature, one is an agricultural product that is directly related to the livelihood of farmers, and the other is a tool for timing, which is especially necessary for life at this time of complex social life. They should be reduced to two-thousandths to comply with the provisions of the outline.

Each Industry Requests Reduction in Business Tax 68

The Ginseng and Bird's Nest Industry Association yesterday submitted a petition stating that the Finance Bureau's request to classify ginseng and bird's nest as common medicines and tax them at a rate of 0.2% was unreasonable. The petition outlined reasons for requesting a re-evaluation, clarifying that these items are not luxury goods, expressing their difficulties, and requesting a reduction in the business tax rate to alleviate the merchants' hardship and prevent business failures.

The association stated that they had read in newspapers that after the tax system was reformed, business tax was levied to compensate for the abolition of "likin" (internal transit tax). The business tax rates were based on the previous income from "likin". The association argued that Shanghai's "likin" revenue was never as substantial as that of other provinces. The current tax rates exceeded the national guidelines, especially for ginseng and bird's nest, which was a fundamental error. The association had submitted two petitions requesting a reduction in the business tax rate, but they were not approved. They felt compelled to list the uses of ginseng and bird's nest, emphasizing that they are life-saving medicines and more important than other medicines. To classify them as luxury goods was a mistake.

The petition further stated that the "Compendium of Materia Medica" details the extensive use of ginseng and bird's nest in various medicinal preparations. They are often used to revive patients at death's door. Wealthy patients may not be affected by the tax, but for the poor, the tax increases the price, potentially leading to their demise. The tax rate for ginseng and bird's nest was higher than other medicines, seemingly focusing only on the wealthy, classifying them as luxury goods and not treating them the same as other medicines. The association implored the authorities to approve the classification of ginseng and bird's nest as medicines, taxed at 0.2%. This would not only alleviate the burden on the industry but also benefit the poor.

The Tea and Food Industry

The draft tax rate proposed for the city listed the tea and food industry at 0.5%. Merchants felt this was unbearable. Besides sending a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, they sent representatives Yang Qixian, Zhu Yongqing, Huang Zhenyu, Chen Hanqing, and others to the Municipal Government and the Finance Bureau to plead their case. Mayor Zhang, Section Chief Shen, and Bureau Chief Cai's representative, Section Chief Ma, received the representatives. The representatives stated the reasons for requesting a lower tax rate as follows:

(1) Tea and food are not luxury goods but common food items for the general public, like salt and rice.

(2) The raw materials for the tea and food industry are similar to those of the pastry and noodle industries, which are taxed at 0.2%. The tea and food industry should have the same tax rate.

(3) The "Nanhua" (Southern Goods) industry, which also sells tea, food, ginseng, bird's nest, and seafood, has a lower tax rate than the tea and food industry.

(4) Besides special taxes, unified taxes, and factory taxes, all raw materials for tea and food are taxed. Imposing a second business tax at such a high rate is unreasonable.

Section Chiefs Shen and Ma stated that the tax rate was only a draft proposal. Because tea and food were considered excessively taxed, they would convey the representatives' opinions to the Mayor and Bureau Chief for consideration and reduction. The representatives were satisfied and left.

The Eyeglasses Industry

The draft regulations and tax rate schedule for the city's business tax have been proposed by the Business Tax Preparation Office of the Municipal Finance Bureau. Because the business tax was a new initiative, they sought opinions from various trade associations through newspaper announcements. The Eyeglasses Trade Association felt that the proposed tax rate of 1% for the eyeglasses industry, the same as luxury goods, was excessive. The association sent Zhuang Honggao, Zhang Shide, and Wang Shuquan as representatives to present their opinions to the office in person and submitted a written petition to reduce the tax rate. The original text is transcribed below:

"Petition to supplement the explanation of the function of eyeglasses for consideration, requesting a reduction in the tax rate to encourage the industry and alleviate merchants' hardship. We have read the First Announcement of your office and learned that the draft regulations and tax rate schedule for the city's business tax have been proposed by your office. Because this is a new initiative, you are seeking opinions from various trade associations. We requested your office to send us the full draft for review. We found that the proposed tax rate for the eyeglasses industry was 1%, which shocked us. Eyeglasses are to the eyes as medicine is to the sick; they are a necessity. The proposed tax rate is the same as that for antiques and gold and silver jewelry. This clearly views eyeglasses as luxury goods and fails to understand their function. Therefore, we venture to briefly explain their effectiveness for your office's consideration.

The form of eyeglasses may vary, but they are mainly used for presbyopia, nearsightedness, and astigmatism. Elderly people suffer from failing eyesight, and presbyopic lenses allow them to see clearly. Nearsighted people cannot see distant objects, but nearsighted lenses allow them to see everything clearly. Young people are often studious, and prolonged viewing can damage their blood. Eyestrain can easily occur, and astigmatic lenses not only benefit hygiene but also provide protection. Colored lenses can block out electric light and sunlight and are suitable for treating eye diseases.

Therefore, eyeglasses are closely related to people's well-being. The eyes are the master of the body. The enjoyment of life depends on the eyes. Ordinary people can see more clearly with eyeglasses, and those with eye diseases are essentially disabled without them. The principles of chemistry and optics cannot function without eyeglasses. The development of industry and science depend on the eyes. Without eyeglasses to protect eyesight, one cannot fully understand the principles.

European and American countries recognize the function of eyeglasses and classify them as medicines. The National Government is implementing business tax to compensate for the loss of "likin" revenue. Shanghai has no "likin" and therefore no loss. Even if regulations are followed, merchants' hardship should be considered, and tax rates should be reduced. The eyeglasses industry should be encouraged and not treated as a luxury.

We hope that your office will adhere to the National Government's principle of creating taxes and adopting the current regulations of Europe and America. We request that the tax rate for eyeglasses be revised to be the same as the 0.2% tax rate for medicines, to benefit the country and its people and avoid the criticism of imposing excessive taxes on merchants. In addition to sending Zhuang Honggao, Zhang Shide, and Wang Shuquan as representatives to present our opinions to your office, we have prepared this document explaining that the function of eyeglasses is different from that of luxury goods and requesting a reduction in the tax rate to encourage the industry. We respectfully submit this petition to the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau Business Tax Preparation Office for review and implementation."

End of quote.

Lin Shi Discusses the Stamp Issue 70

Stated that he was acting under orders

According to Guomin News Agency, there have been widespread discussions regarding the opposition from the Printing Bureau of the Ministry of Finance in Beiping to the Directorate General of Posts' ordering of stamps from foreign companies. The agency's reporter visited Lin Shi, the former Director General of Posts, to inquire about the matter. Lin Shi, though unwell, received the reporter and discussed the issue.

Reporter: It is said that the contract between the Ministry of Communications and the foreign company for ordering stamps was advocated by you last year when you served concurrently as Director of the Postal Department. Is this true?

Lin Shi appeared surprised and shook his head, stating that there were many misunderstandings regarding this matter. He clarified that he did not advocate this while concurrently serving as Director of the Postal Department. Furthermore, his concurrent service as Director of the Postal Department was not last year, as he had relinquished the position in the previous year.

Reporter: Then why did the Post Office contract with a foreign company? What was the process?

Lin Shi: When I was Director General of Posts, I was acting under orders regarding the contract with a foreign company. The accusations against me are not true. I have already made a statement on this matter. However, the process is quite lengthy. Since the autumn of the 18th year, I have suffered from dysentery and have been ill for over a year. Recently, I have been losing blood, making it very difficult to speak. I apologize that I cannot provide a detailed answer at this time and will do so after I have recovered.

The reporter, seeing that Lin Shi was very weak, did not want to cause further strain and excused himself.

Joint Meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of the Lawyers Association 72

(1) The Shanghai District Court and the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court issued an order suggesting that the use of service be changed. If service is required, it must be stated in writing, otherwise the old rules will still apply. It was resolved to inform all members to take note.

Families of Victims of the Dachang Steamer Disaster Establish an Association 73

Requesting Support from All Sectors

The families of the victims of the Dachang Steamer disaster established the Dachang Steamer Victims' Families Association on May 3. The association issued an appeal to all sectors of society:

"The Dahua Company's Dachang Steamer departed from Dapukaishi, Haizhou, on April 13 at 3:15 AM, heading for Shanghai. At 8:30 PM the next day, outside the Wusongkou, it encountered the Ping'an Company's Dahua Steamer. The Dachang Steamer sounded its horn to warn the other ship, as per usual procedure. However, the captain and first and second mates of the Dahua Steamer were not on duty at the time, and only the helmsman was present (as determined after the fact). Therefore, the Dahua Steamer did not respond to the Dachang Steamer's horn. After sounding the horn again, the Dahua Steamer still did not respond and rammed the Dahua Steamer broadside, penetrating the engine room. The Dachang Steamer was struck on its left side, where the red light was hung. The Dahua Steamer did not turn its bow to the right but rammed the red light side of the other ship's broadside. Anyone familiar with navigation knows that this was a driving error. The Dachang Steamer sustained a massive breach, and seawater immediately flooded in.

After causing the accident, the Dahua Steamer not only did not help but sped away. The Dachang Steamer urgently sounded its distress horn and fired distress flares. The crew and passengers shouted for help. The surrounding sea area and the Wusong Fort were all aware of the situation. The Dahua Steamer then realized that even if it tried to escape, it could not hide from observers. It returned, but about five to six minutes had elapsed since the initial accident. The Dahua Steamer still did not help but stood by and watched. It circled the Dachang Steamer three times. All who saw it were filled with hatred, and heaven and earth could not tolerate it. Fortunately, the Taigu Company's Hanyang Steamer heard the distress calls and came to help at around 9:40 PM. When the Dahua Steamer saw a third party arrive, it grudgingly provided assistance, but it had spent over an hour watching from the sidelines. Five minutes after it began to help, the Dachang Steamer sank entirely, drowning seven crew members and dozens of passengers.

The Dahua Steamer's negligence caused the accident, and its deliberate inaction afterward contributed to the tragedy. According to civil and criminal law, the Dahua Steamer is fully responsible. The families of the dozens of victims on the Dachang Steamer have lost their support and become orphans. We have been negotiating with the Ping'an Company regarding compensation and the aftermath, but there have been no results. We have entrusted lawyers Zhang Zhirang and Jiang Qishi to protect our rights according to law. We ask all sectors of society and all public organizations to uphold justice and provide support to comfort the deceased and reassure the helpless."

Meeting Record of the Anhui Rice Merchants Association 74

The Anhui Rice Merchants Association of this port held a meeting of the Standing Committee yesterday afternoon. Attending were Lin Chunyu, Yan Zhishan, and Executive Committee members Wang Yuelou and Lin Songru, along with ten others. Lin Chunyu was elected chairman and proposed the following items:

(1) Transportation companies assign personnel to take care of passengers and goods transported from Beijing to Shanghai. This is their due duty, and there should be no charge for this. Due to the large number of personnel at the upper station, a fee of one jiao (ten cents) per ton was requested. This was not done for many years, but now the fee has suddenly increased by five fen (five cents) per ton. The committee unanimously rejected this increase.

(2) It was previously agreed with the Ren Grain Association that payments for hulled rice should be made within ten days. Some are arbitrarily delaying payments, causing losses to the customers. This is not acceptable and a solution must be found.

(3) Recently, letters have been received from various inland groups saying that this year's wheat harvest is very good, unprecedented in recent years. With the harvest approaching and foreign wheat flooding the country, there is concern that the market will weaken if measures are not taken to remove mud and deduct pounds. The committee resolved to send letters to various groups urging them to rectify the situation.

Eighth District Party Headquarters Requests 82

Rectification of the Songhu Branch Road

Request to Restore the Number of Train Services

The Wusong Eighth District Party Headquarters submitted a petition to the Municipal Party Headquarters, requesting that it be forwarded to the National Government to order the Ministry of Railways to quickly rectify the Songhu Branch Road. The original petition is recorded below:

"Petition regarding the request for rectification. The Songhu Railway is the only major transportation route between Wusong and Shanghai. Since the introduction of steam trains, trains have often been delayed or cancelled. Changes in schedules and reduced services have caused crowding and complaints. Not only have passengers suffered, but all parties have suffered greatly. If this is not quickly rectified, the impact will be unimaginable. Social progress requires increased transportation. Train services should be increased based on actual needs and should not be arbitrarily reduced. This is the general principle. There were public buses between Shanghai and Jiangwan, but now the number of services has been increased. There are no public buses between Shanghai and Wusong, and train services have been reduced. This is unreasonable. The representatives of the district unanimously resolved to request the central government to order the Ministry of Railways to quickly rectify the Songwan Railway and restore the original number of services. We respectfully submit this petition for your review and referral."

Kang-Tibetan Walking Tour

Certificates and Passports All Obtained

Regarding reports in various newspapers the day before yesterday about the organization of the Kang-Tibetan Walking Tour, a reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency inquired at the tour's office whether the organization was the same as the one formed in August of last year. They happened to meet Mr. Wang Jin-yuan, the tour's secretary, who said, "Our group was indeed organized in August of last year. Its purpose is to study the history, geography, people's customs, cultural development, resources, transportation, trade, and current situation of the border between Tibet and India, and to awaken them to the British encroachment on the frontier. We aim to conduct a detailed investigation and present it to the nation to reveal the truth of British aggression on the borders and to help open up the Tibetan source in the future. We could have set off earlier, but due to various reasons such as recruiting talent, contacting for passports, raising funds, etc., we petitioned in Beijing in November of last year. We have now received encouragement and instructions from Chairman Chiang, Vice Commander Zhang, and celebrities from all walks of life.
