Cycling Traveler 84

Fortunately Meets an Ethical Thief

Inscriptions from Celebrities and Travel Certificates Returned

Wei Juezhong, the cyclist who travels the world alone, stayed at 932 Zhenru Railway Station Road a month ago, immersing himself in writing. On March 10th, his leather suitcase was stolen. He reported the theft to the Zhenru Public Security Bureau, and it was recorded in various newspapers. Unexpectedly, at around 9 a.m. the day before yesterday, Mr. Wei received a large envelope from the Zhenru Post Office without postage. Upon opening it, he found the celebrity inscriptions and travel certificates that had been stolen the previous month. At the bottom was written "Sent from this city." On the front left end of the envelope, there were four characters written in pen: "Conscience Discovered." On the back lower end, there were two lines of small writing in pen: "Please forgive me, I didn't have money to put on stamps." And "You must thank me in the newspaper when you receive this, if it wasn't for my means, you probably wouldn't have this success." The handwriting was neat and undoubtedly written by the ethical thief himself. Mr. Wei was overjoyed upon receiving it and thanked endlessly. According to Mr. Wei, in addition to these two important items, there were also landscape photo negatives and manuscripts in the stolen suitcase. If the ethical thief discovers his conscience again and returns them one by one, he will express his gratitude in Shanghai newspapers.

University Student Disappears 85

Wife and Sister in Dispute

Sister Accused of Occupying Property

Wife's Identity Questioned

Ni Guangxun, a student at Chizhi University, suddenly left home last winter and his whereabouts are unknown. Later, it was heard that Ni had gone to Peiping alone to study at Yenching University, but his family has not received any communication from Ni since his disappearance, so it is difficult to determine whether he is studying in Peiping. Recently, Fan Abao, who claims to be Ni's wife, filed a complaint with the Special District Local Court, accusing Ni's sister, Zeng Ni Guangchen (the sixth sister), of occupying Guangxun's 20,000 yuan family property. The Special Court had once summoned them for questioning, but because the plaintiff had not paid the litigation fees, the judge ordered her to pay the fees before summoning witnesses for further interrogation. Now, the defendant, Zeng Ni Guangchen, hired two lawyers, Zhang Deqin and Shen Yuesheng, to submit a response stating that Ni Guangxun is only 24 years old and was studying at Chizhi University. Whether he secretly went to Peiping to study is difficult to determine. However, according to the defendant and Ni's relatives, before Guangxun left, they never heard of him marrying or participating in a wedding on any date. Therefore, the plaintiff's identity is unclear and suspicious, and she should not expect to inherit any of Guangxun's property. The reason why the plaintiff has this improper idea to take a chance is that the defendant's late father did hire Fan Abao as a servant when he was alive. Perhaps Guangxun had an improper relationship with the plaintiff at that time, and it was only an act of indecency. This should only be regarded as Guangxun's personal emotional entanglement, which should be negotiated with Guangxun himself. The defendant or relatives cannot be forced to recognize her as Guangxun's formal wife and demand that the defendant inherit Guangxun's property. The meaning is very clear. Therefore, if the plaintiff wants to claim property rights, she must first determine her identity. Now, the plaintiff is arbitrarily making trouble without reason, which is a fundamental mistake and cannot be tolerated in law or reason. The plaintiff's accusation of occupying family property and refusing to hand it over is even more unreasonable and absurd. The defendant's late father passed away in the 18th year of the Republic of China. At that time, Guangxun was already 22 years old and an adult, not a young child without knowledge. When the father was alive, he worked in the customs office and his monthly income was only enough for household expenses. He did not engage in other side businesses to become wealthy. Perhaps there were slight savings, but the expenses for Guangxun's years of schooling and the other two brothers' schooling were also used up over time. Moreover, the defendant is Guangxun's sister. Is Guangxun the only one who has the right to inherit the father's estate? Can't the defendant and the other two brothers intervene? According to the law, they should inherit and share. Now, the plaintiff does not understand the truth and falsely claims that Guangxun's property is stored with the defendant, which is completely slanderous and fabricated in the hope of taking a chance. It should be known that Guangxun is already an adult, not like a child who must have his property kept by others. Who would willingly give up his ownership and not manage it himself, but have to rely on others? Furthermore, the plaintiff's statement that Guangxun and she have always had a harmonious relationship is even more ridiculous and absurd. If Guangxun and she were extremely in love, why did he leave without saying a word, regardless of everything? It can be predicted that Guangxun's situation at the time must have been unpleasant and with unspeakable pain, so he took this last resort. This is not something the defendant could have imagined. In short, the plaintiff's statements are completely wishful thinking and fabricated out of thin air. Since there is no conclusive evidence, how can she make demands on the defendant to inherit Guangxun's property? Based on the above facts, it is clear that the plaintiff's lawsuit has no reason and is deliberately harassing. Therefore, she filed a lawsuit requesting dismissal and judgment to bear the litigation costs. However, Fan Abao, during the previous court hearing, mentioned Ni Wenming, Guangxun's uncle, as a witness to prove that she was Ni Guangxun's wife. Therefore, how Fan and Ni combined will be determined when Ni's uncle is summoned for a subsequent hearing, which may prove it.

Son of Famous Doctor 86

Divorces Due to Impotence

Alimony and Dowry Fees

Must Compensate 5,500 Yuan

Tao Yiqing, the eldest son of the late famous doctor Tao Yinkang of this city, was recently sued in the local court by his wife, Tao Cai Wenqing, for abuse and abandonment, and accused Tao of suffering from impotence, demanding a divorce and claiming compensation of 8,000 yuan for consolation money and 1,977 yuan for dowry fees. After multiple summons, the case was not concluded. The day before yesterday, a continuation hearing was held in the afternoon by Judge Chen Bingxin in the Sixth Court. Both parties attended with their lawyers. Tao Yiqing first stated that her (referring to the plaintiff) accusation that I have impotence is false. The money needed for my marriage with her was borrowed from relatives and friends. Soon after, my late father, Yinkang, passed away, which led to debt collectors constantly knocking on the door. Therefore, the environment was extremely bad, and I suffered a great shock mentally. Unfortunately, after this divorce lawsuit occurred, my reputation and business suffered a significant impact, so I do not want a divorce. The court said, "She doesn't want to be with you. What's the point of forcing her to live with you?" (Answer) "If she insists on leaving, I have no choice. However, I am really unable to bear the alimony. As for the dowry, I will return it as listed on her list, and compensate for the missing items with money." Next, Tao Cai Wenqing stated that what the defendant said was all lies. Whether he has a hidden illness is proven by the Chinese Red Cross Hospital's certificate. He is truly heartless, delaying my life and cutting off my livelihood. If I continue to live with him, my lifelong happiness will be exploited by him. Before I married, I relied on my parents. After marriage, I should be protected by my husband. Moreover, my father and brothers are poor. The cost of buying various dowry items for over 1,000 yuan when I got married was not easy. If I am penniless after the divorce, how will I live? Therefore, the pain I have suffered and my future life require no less than 8,000 yuan. The judge attempted to reconcile the situation in court, but because the defendant firmly refused, the reconciliation failed. The judge then invited Prosecutor Wang to express his opinion, stating that the plaintiff's request for divorce is justified because the defendant's hidden illness has been confirmed by the hospital. Please make a judgment in accordance with the law. Finally, after mutual arguments by the two lawyers, the judge concluded and adjourned the court to await the verdict. The verdict has been recorded as follows: The marriage between the plaintiff (Tao Cai Wenqing) and the defendant (Tao Yiqing) should be dissolved. The defendant should pay the plaintiff 5,500 yuan for alimony and dowry clothing. The plaintiff's other claims are dismissed. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

Two Unemployed Attempt Suicide 87

Fortunately, Both Were Rescued

Xie Zhouzhou, a young man wearing Western clothing, threw himself into the river at the Tongxing Wharf on Wusong Wai Ma Road at 9:50 p.m. the night before last, attempting suicide. Constable Hou Desheng from the First Precinct of the Seventh District Public Security Bureau spotted him and immediately stepped forward to rescue him. With the help of boatmen, he was rescued and brought back to the precinct. After questioning by Director Zhang, he identified himself as Xie Zhouzhou, 20 years old, from Wuxi, Jiangsu. He used to work for a Westerner, but had been unemployed for over a year since the Westerner returned to his country in February of last year. With no means of making a living, his finances deteriorated day by day. The bleak future left him with no foothold, and he had no choice but to take a train from Shanghai to Wusong and throw himself into the river. He requested resettlement after being rescued. Director Zhang, after taking his statement, noted that his name, Zhouzhou, was unfamiliar. After checking the dictionary, it roughly meant resentment for his own inability. When asked about the meaning, he replied that the name had been used for a long time and had no other meaning. After the statement, he ordered the police to send him to the judicial section for disposition yesterday.

Huang Fuquan, a patrol officer from the Wusong Seventh District Public Security Bureau, was patrolling the Paotaiwan area at around 2 p.m. the day before yesterday when he suddenly saw a man pacing back and forth on the beach, sighing with a miserable expression. After looking around, he made a gesture of throwing himself into the sea. Seeing this, the patrol officer rushed forward and grabbed the man's clothes, preventing him from falling into the water. He was then taken back to the district office. After questioning by District Chief Zhao Ze Zhou, the man identified himself as Huang Fuquan, 28 years old, living in Bailu Lane, Broadway Road, Shanghai. He used to work on a ship, but recently became unemployed and could not maintain his livelihood. He thought it would be better to die than to suffer in this world, so he took a car to Songjiang, hoping to commit suicide by throwing himself into the sea. While giving his statement, he was weeping, which moved those who heard it. After much persuasion, the police were sent to Shanghai to notify his family. That night, his father, Huang Tulin, came to Songjiang and presented himself to the Seventh District to take him home.

Beside the Body 88

A Love Letter

Not Dead for Love

Cause of Suicide Unknown

At around 8 a.m. yesterday morning, a young man's body suddenly floated up on the riverbank outside Suzhou Creek Park. He was wearing a tweed hunting jacket, black trousers, black leather shoes, and leather leggings. He had a white ring on his finger, with indistinguishable gold and silver, engraved with the blue Western letters "CK." He appeared to be in his early twenties. A Chinese constable, number 68, from the Customs Water Police Station discovered it and fished the body back to the police station. A love letter was found on the body, along with several pawn tickets from the Liyu Guest House at 2 Alley, Fuyu Lane, telephone number 61315, and a delivery order from various companies for a black and gray tweed hunting jacket costing 11.50 yuan. The police station then transferred the body and belongings to the Nanshi Lifesaving Bureau's patrol boat for collection, pending identification. The love letter was written in pencil on a Chinese-style letterhead and addressed to a certain lane, number 18, North Sichuan Road. The original text, which was read with deep affection and reluctance to part, indicated that the deceased did not commit suicide for love. The following is a copy:

"My dearest ○○ sister,

Everything you said in Beijing the day before yesterday, I naturally understand. I originally wanted to write to you, but there was nothing going on at home. Please forgive me, ○ sister. I am going to Nanjing on May 3rd. I will wait for you at the Xinguang Theater at 6:30 p.m. the day after tomorrow. Please don't miss the appointment. Oh sister, I am about to leave you, but you don't have to be sad. I believe in you and love you. But I hope you will take care of everything after I leave and not always think of me. Communicate with me often. You once said you wanted to send a small photo. I am very grateful to you. I am really embarrassed and dare not accept your kindness. I don't know how to repay your affection, ○ sister. After arriving in Nanjing, I will report everything to you. I will write to you then. Now there are other things and I can't write more. Let's talk the day after tomorrow. Say you are progressing greatly. Your lover, Fan Mingde."

Municipal Utilities Bureau Urges 89

Improvement of Voltage on Dong Yokohama Road

In the past few months, the voltage in the Dong Yokohama Road area of ​​Zhabei has been too low and unstable, causing the electric lights to flicker like candles in the wind, which has caused great suffering to residents. The Municipal Utilities Bureau, upon receiving the report, sent personnel to use an automatic voltage recording meter to obtain a 24-hour voltage record of the area. The highest voltage was 214 volts, and the time was from 1:00 a.m. to 6:30 a.m. The lowest voltage was 154 volts, and the time was from 6:00 p.m. to 9:00 p.m. The fluctuations in between were very drastic, with drops of 100 volts or more in an instant. The fluctuations were slight only from 12:00 noon to 1:00 p.m. The reason was that there were many power users in the vicinity, which had such a significant impact. The Zhabei Water and Electricity Company was often asked to replace the main line on the road with a thicker one or reconnect it to the Baoshan Road main line. If the voltage was still too low and unstable, or the Baoshan Road main line could not bear the load, a transformer substation would be set up near Dong Yokohama Road to supply power. It is now known that the company has immediately added a set of feeder lines, and the voltage is slightly higher than before, but still not very stable. It is planning to add a transformer near the Continental Lane on Dong Yokohama Road, which can also feed power to Dingxing Lane on North Sichuan Road and Yingui Road, etc. Because the 6,600-volt high-voltage line has to pass through the Songhu Railway, permission has been obtained from the Railway Bureau, and pole erection is underway, which is about to be completed. The voltage in the Dong Yokohama area will soon meet the needs of the public.

Japanese 90

Candy Leader Mr. Morinaga Visits Shanghai

The Shanghai Confectionery and Biscuit Association hosted a banquet the night before last to welcome Mr. Taichiro Morinaga, president of Morinaga Confectionery Co., Ltd. of Tokyo, Japan, a world-renowned candy factory that sells its products all over the world. Mr. Morinaga has more than 50 years of experience in manufacturing candy and advocates open special manufacturing methods without being secretive. He came to Shanghai this time to inspect the candy industry in China. Executive members of the Shanghai Confectionery, Biscuit, and Canned Food Industry Association, including Xi Guansheng, Le Fucheng, Xu Wenbin, Li Yuxuan, and Tu Kaizheng, held a banquet at the Xinghualou Restaurant on Simalu the night before last to welcome him, and invited all members to accompany him, with more than 70 people in attendance. Mr. Morinaga, accompanied by his secretary, Masakiyo Saito, translator, Seiichi Hayashida, and manager of the Shanghai agency, Sojiro Mori, took their seats at 8:00 p.m. First, Chairman Zhang Yichen delivered a welcome speech, followed by Zhu Xiaoyun reading a welcome address. Then, Mr. Morinaga gave a sincere speech, stating that China and Japan are brotherly countries, and candy is also a staple food for the people. In the past 20 years, the sentiment towards candy in Japan has become extremely strong, and the social demand is high, occupying an important position in the Japanese industry. He was very pleased to be welcomed by his colleagues in your country, and hoped that the Chinese and Japanese confectionery industries would join hands in the future to promote the progress of the Eastern food industry, and hoped that his colleagues present today would visit Japan. Finally, Xi Guansheng gave a speech, and the gathering ended joyfully at 10:00 p.m. It was also heard that the industry association presented a silk banner with the inscription "Leader of Modern Candy" to express their respect and commemorate the occasion.

In the Chuanlu Lawsuit 91

Feng Lizhou Guilty of Defamation

Fined Fifty Yuan

Zhang Taikai, the former general manager of Chuanlu Company, was prosecuted by the Shanghai Local Court for embezzling more than 300,000 yuan of public funds and sentenced to imprisonment. He died of illness in prison last month. Since the Zhang case occurred, senior personnel of the road, including Zeng Xianzhi, Ni Gongwei, Feng Lizhou, and Zou Yunchun, have been at odds with each other and have been involved in lawsuits in the Special District Local Court, either accusing them of concealing criminals or accusing them of defamation. The Special Court has held separate hearings to investigate each case. Now, one case has been concluded. The day before yesterday, Judge Xun pronounced the verdict, finding Feng Lizhou guilty of defamation and fining him 50 yuan. If he fails to pay the fine, he will be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. The other defendants, Zou Yunchun, Zeng Xianzhi, and Ni Gongwei, were all found not guilty. Another case of Feng accusing Zeng Xianzhi of concealing criminals has not yet been concluded.

Chauffeur Recognizes Robbers 92

Finally Visited and Captured

Multiple People Detained

Qiu Mujin, the compradore of Taigu Company's Wuchang steamboat, had his residence at 44 Junhe Lane, Alabaster Road, broken into by several armed robbers at 10 a.m. on the 30th of last month, who looted more than 6,100 yuan of property and a Mauser pistol for self-defense. Because Qiu's chauffeur, Li Lingen, secretly observed the robbers' faces during the robbery and felt that he could recognize them if he saw them again, the Huishi police station dispatched detective Shang Wu and detective Chen Dabao, who immediately took Li to various public places to secretly investigate. At 9 p.m. the next night, they saw a male and female tourist pair walking out of the Yong'an Company's rooftop garden. Li believed that the male was indeed the robber who committed the crime at the scene, so the detective secretly followed him and saw him enter room number 4 of the Anle Palace Hotel on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession. The detective then asked the French police to dispatch detectives to rush to the scene and arrest the man. He identified himself as Chen Gengsheng from Changzhou, and said that his accomplices, Zheng Guifu and Zheng Fuchang from Haimen, were bathing at the Longquan Bathhouse at 571 Zhejiang Road. The detectives rushed there and arrested them. 130 yuan in banknotes and five Han banknotes of one yuan each, a watch, and a gold ring were found on the two Zhengs. The plaintiff identified them as the original stolen goods. The day before yesterday morning, Chen Gengsheng also confessed in court the names of several accomplices who went to rob, including Fang Amao, Xu A'gen, and Fang Jinsheng, saying that after the fact, the spoils were divided, with each share being 70 yuan. Fang Amao had two pistols, so he got three shares. Xu A'gen also got three shares. The stolen jewelry was sold by Xu and Fang's wives. My uncle, A'er, worked as a chauffeur at Qiu's house. I often went to Qiu's house, and the gate was very strict. Only acquaintances would open the door. I didn't go with them when they robbed, but I got 55 yuan, a watch, and a gold ring after the fact. Zheng Fuchang confessed that Guifu was my son. I came to Shanghai from my hometown to find my son and go home. I did not participate in the robbery. Judge Wu ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody for a subsequent hearing at a later date.

Tenants of Lizhong Lane Oppose Rent Increase 93

All 140 tenant households in Lizhong Lane in this city have united to oppose the rent increase by landlord Chen Changkun and have filed a lawsuit with the Shanghai Local Court requesting the validity of the contract. The court has conducted hearings on the various situations, which have been reported in this newspaper. The following is an excerpt of the key points of the response by the plaintiff tenant representatives, such as Zhu Wenxin, to the defendant Chen Changkun's counterclaim: (1) The only reason for the counterclaim is that the price of gold has soared. In fact, what does the rise and fall of the price of gold have to do with housing? The rent calculation should of course be based on the cost or purchase price. The so-called annual loss of more than 4,100 taels is unknown how it is calculated. Could it be that the cost also fluctuates with the price of gold from time to time? (2) Chen Changkun knows the previous rent amount of Lizhong Lane like the back of his hand and knows everything, but he evades and refuses to acknowledge the obligations of the written contract with Jukangzhuang, which is self-contradictory and ridiculous. (3) Regarding the part of the rent arrears, the tenants in this lane have already obtained the contract with Jukangzhuang in advance. There is no reason to increase the rent during the limited period. If the rent increase can be canceled, it will of course be paid in full.

Detective's Mistress's Diamond Ring 94

Was a Gift from a Robber

Involved After the Case

Zhang Limei, the mistress of detective Hu Baoxiang, is 37 years old and has a charming appearance. Because Hu has a legal family, he hid her in number 2, Wufeng Lane, French Concession. The woman was acquainted with Zhang Dianjia. This time, Zhang and his gang robbed the resident Fang Changqing at 3 and a half Danshui Road, Gu Wang at 1032 Avenue Edward VII, Lu Wang at 1510, and Jin Hailou, a passerby who was robbed on Yunnan Road, Hankou Road. The loot was very large, so he gave a diamond ring to the woman. Recently, Zhang and his gang were arrested by the Huishi police station and confessed to giving away the stolen goods. Detectives Zhang Bingcheng, Ding Baoxiang, etc. went to the French Concession the day before yesterday and arrested Zhang Limei and brought her to the Special District Local Court. Judge Ge questioned the woman, who admitted that she had received the ring as a gift, but said that she did not know its authenticity at the time. She took it to a pawn shop for appraisal, and it was said to be an "压鼎" (a cheap ring). Then Hu Baoxiang took it away, and now he doesn't know where he threw it. Judge Ge then ordered the woman to be remanded in custody pending Hu Baoxiang's arrival and interrogation.

Special Meeting of the Cattle and Sheep Industry Guild 96

Joint Petition to Abolish Inspection Fees

Request for Exemption from Retroactive Approval for the 19th Year

The Shanghai Cattle and Sheep Industry Guild convened a special meeting yesterday at 2:00 PM, attended by over 530 members, due to the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau's order for the guild to pay overdue duplicate inspection fees for cattle and sheep for the 19th year. Chairman Chen Guanghai first reported that the Finance Bureau held a second meeting on April 16th to pursue the overdue inspection fees for the 19th year. Wang, the section chief of the Finance Bureau, stated that the Health Bureau's inspection count for the 19th year showed over 80,000 heads of cattle, which was 20,000 fewer than the Finance Bureau's count. The veterinary inspection count and the registered list would be used as the standard for cattle calculation to ensure fairness. The guild listed the actual situation of repeated drafting of inspection forms. At the previous meeting, the Health Bureau also stated that some repetitions were unavoidable, and that cattle for work, dairy, and transit, as well as sheep, were not slaughtered in the city and should not be charged fees. The calculation of 30 cents per calf should also be lowered. Yan, the representative of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, also stated that the guild was a legal entity among the industry, and that the inspection fees were apportioned and collected, so the Finance Bureau should understand the situation and exempt the guild from retroactive apportionment. There was no substantial outcome at the meeting. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has now forwarded a letter from the Finance Bureau with meeting minutes. The minutes failed to fully record the guild's statements regarding repeated drafting of inspection forms, the fact that cattle not slaughtered in the city should not be charged, and that the 30 cents per calf should be reduced. The issue of retroactive payment for the 19th year and this year's fees should be expressed. Subsequently, Zhang Wenbie of the Yellow Cattle industry and Chen Baosheng of the Goat industry proposed that the last time, colleagues especially supported the request for the government to stop collecting inspection fees, with the pig, cattle, and sheep industries undertaking the administrative expenses for livestock inspection. The chairman expressed agreement. Now that the national government has abolished exorbitant taxes and resolutely cut surtaxes to implement new business taxes, and the Ministry of Finance has notified all municipal, provincial, and county agencies that they must not collect fees similar to surtaxes or transit taxes under any name, and that those already in place should be abolished and those not yet in place should not be created. The slaughtering industry already bears slaughter taxes and now has inspection fees added, which is an unbearable burden. Moreover, new business taxes will be implemented soon. If the Director of the Municipal Finance Bureau can follow the teachings of Sun Yat-sen, he should abolish these inspection fees similar to surtaxes as soon as possible to uphold the principle of one tax per item. If the expenses for livestock inspection need to be covered, then the cattle, sheep, and pig industries can undertake them. Moreover, municipal business taxes will be implemented soon to offset the costs. The chairman suggested that since the industry guild has not been understood by the Finance Bureau, the cattle and sheep merchants should jointly petition the municipal government for survival. If the municipal government cannot understand, then they should petition the national government and various ministries. Subsequently, Yao Changsheng of the Calf industry and Chen Baosheng of the Goat industry proposed that Articles 7, 8, 9, and 3 of the slaughter inspection rules were extremely harsh and should be amended. A resolution was made to request the government to amend them. Chairman Chen Guanghai said that the Finance Bureau's pursuit of the inspection fees for the 19th year should follow the method of the second meeting, listing the repeated items and submitting them to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward to the Finance Bureau, requesting understanding and exemption from retroactive payment. Regarding the petition, the guild was not in a position to lead it at present. Subsequently, Zhang Wenbie of the Yellow Cattle industry, Chen Baosheng of the Goat industry, You Zengfa of the Lake Sheep industry, Yao Changsheng of the Calf industry, and Jiang Fanglai and Fei Shaojin of this operation all advocated that the petition should be carried out immediately. As a result of the discussion, it was resolved that the guild should submit a request to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward to the Finance Bureau for exemption from retroactive payment, and that the gold entity cattle and sheep industries should contact the pig industry to jointly petition for the abolition of pig, cattle, and sheep inspection fees.

Publication of New Theories of Modern Economics 97

Edited by the Jiaotong University Economics Society

The Jiaotong University Economics Society has consistently strived for academic research. Its publications over the years, such as the Economic Weekly (formerly a supplement to the Shishi Xinbao, now independently published by the society, with 42 issues already published), the Economic Review, and the National Railway Overview, have all been meticulously compiled and are invaluable works. Since their publication, they have been highly praised by society. Recently, Cheng Zhizheng, the Minister of Publications of the Society, has compiled dozens of graduate theses and other works into a book titled "New Theories of Modern Economics," published by Guangyi Bookstore. It has already been published, with inscriptions by Minister Sun Zhesheng and Mr. Ye Gongchao, and prefaces by various celebrities. The content and appearance are extremely exquisite. Important papers include "Discussion on the Price Ratio of Gold and Silver," "Study of the Central Banks of Five Countries: England, America, Germany, France, and Japan," "The Current Situation of Industries in Eastern Provinces," "Overview of Unemployment Relief Methods in England, Germany, and the United States," "Public Utilities," and "The Manchurian Question," totaling over 300,000 words. The book is divided into two large volumes and priced at 2.4 yuan. It is currently sold at a cheap price of only 40% off. Those concerned with economics should not miss having a copy.

The English translation of Sun Yat-sen's Doctrine, published by the Shanghai Yinghua Independent Weekly, has now been released. Meeting Minutes of the Huaxinfang Housing Association 105

The Yangshupu Road Huaxinfang Tenant Union held its second executive committee meeting at 9:00 AM yesterday. Chairman Hu Junjie chaired the meeting. Matters for discussion: (1) Two letters were sent to Yizhongyin Company, but no reply was received. How should this be handled? The executive committee members spoke one after another, saying that since the company did not reply, it should be regarded as tacitly agreeing to cancel the rent increase. Although there was a letter to Lu Fengming personally, it did not mention canceling the rent increase, which showed that the company had no intention of making concessions. (B) Before the company expresses its refusal to cancel the rent increase, the elected economic custodians will deposit the payable rent in the bank and file with the party, government, and judicial authorities and publish a statement in the newspaper. (2) (Omitted). (3) Other business houses in the urban area are separately contacting the Management Office, but since the properties belong to the same owner, they should not be divided. It is proposed to notify the business houses to join the association and proceed uniformly. It was resolved to approve. (4) It is requested that the economic funding cannot be arranged, and that each household should temporarily pay one silver dollar to facilitate the association's work. It was resolved to approve the retroactive recognition. At the temporary proposal, Yi Xia Yongchao proposed that the committee members of the association should not be allocated, and that the standing chairman should be able to hire people as necessary. The resolution was passed, and the meeting adjourned.

Weather Report 107

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the skies over the Yangtze River basin and coastal areas are cloudy. There is rain south of the Taiwan Strait. There is a strong southeasterly wind on the East China Sea, and the wind direction on the Yellow Sea is uncertain. The highest temperature in this port in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 76.9 degrees Fahrenheit, and the lowest was 49.7 degrees Fahrenheit. The highest temperature on the same day last year was 65.1 degrees Fahrenheit.
